System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To make a decision on which route to choose, let's break down the factors influencing each route's cost:

1. **Route O-L-D**:
   - Cost per driver on segment O-L: 10 * X, where X is the number of drivers choosing this route.
   - Fixed cost for segment L-D: 210.

   Total cost for choosing O-L-D is `10X + 210`.

2. **Route O-R-D**:
   - Fixed cost for segment O-R: 210.
   - Cost per driver on segment R-D: 10 * Y, where Y is the number of drivers choosing this route.

   Total cost for choosing O-R-D is `210 + 10Y`.

The goal is to minimize the cost, maximizing the payoff from the 400 point endowment. Here are some strategies or considerations:

- If more drivers choose O-L-D, the cost for each driver on segment O-L will increase significantly. In this situation, O-R-D may be more cost-effective since segment R-D cost is shared with fewer drivers.
- Conversely, if O-R-D becomes crowded, its cost might go up, making O-L-D potentially cheaper.
- Equilibrium can occur where both routes offer similar costs based on driver distribution adjusting in response to previous rounds.

Without insights into other drivers' behaviors or the distribution in prior rounds, an initial choice would be speculative.

Considering the rules and the nature of such balancing games, starting with less crowded routes traditionally provides a better cost benefit. However, we do not have initial distribution data, so a balanced opening strategy could involve starting with O-R-D due to its stable base cost and assess from there.

Based on this analysis, I would choose:

```json
{"route": "O-R-D"}
```

Human: You are agent 12.
Summary of previous round:
  Your Choice: O-R-D
  Route Choice Distribution: {'O-L-D': 4, 'O-R-D': 14}
  Your Regret: 90


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: Let's analyze the situation based on the previous round and adjust the strategy accordingly:

1. **Review of Previous Round:**
   - You chose route O-R-D.
   - Distribution was 4 drivers on O-L-D and 14 drivers on O-R-D.
   - Your regret was 90, indicating that the cost of the route you chose was higher than that of the other route by 90 points.

2. **Cost Calculations for the Previous Round:**
   - For O-R-D: 
     - Fixed cost on O-R: 210.
     - Variable cost on R-D: 10 * 14 = 140.
     - Total cost: 210 + 140 = 350.

   - For O-L-D:
     - Variable cost on O-L: 10 * 4 = 40.
     - Fixed cost on L-D: 210.
     - Total cost: 40 + 210 = 250.

3. **Understanding Regret:**
   - Since your regret was 90, the alternative route (O-L-D) would have cost you 90 points less than the route you chose.
   - Given the calculations, O-L-D was indeed cheaper in the previous round (250 vs. 350).

4. **Decision for the Current Round:**
   - If the distribution remains similar and more drivers continue choosing O-R-D, the cost will likely remain higher.
   - Thus, shifting to O-L-D could be advantageous as it was cheaper last round.

5. **Considerations:**
   - Players may adjust based on their own regrets, but if tendencies remain, favoring the less populated route may yield better results.

Based on this analysis, switching to route O-L-D seems to be a prudent choice to minimize costs in the upcoming round, assuming similar distribution among routes persists:

```json
{"route": "O-L-D"}
```

  Your Choice: O-R-D

  Your Regret: 150


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: Let's evaluate the situation from the previous round and plan the strategy for the current round:

1. **Review of Previous Round:**
   - You chose route O-R-D.
   - Route choice distribution was heavily skewed: 17 drivers on O-R-D and 1 driver on O-L-D.
   - Your regret was 150, suggesting that choosing O-L-D would have cost 150 points less than O-R-D.

2. **Cost Calculations for the Previous Round:**
   - For O-R-D:
     - Fixed cost on O-R: 210.
     - Variable cost on R-D: 10 * 17 = 170.
     - Total cost: 210 + 170 = 380.

   - For O-L-D (based on regret analysis):
     - Given the regret of 150, the cost for O-L-D would be 380 - 150 = 230.
     - Recapping: Variable cost on O-L for 1 person: 10 * 1 = 10.
     - Fixed cost on L-D: 210.
     - Total cost: 10 + 210 = 220 (corrected based on assumed near calculations).

3. **Understanding Regret:**
   - Your regret indicates that O-L-D was much cheaper in retrospect, corroborating with the sole user having benefited from significant savings.
   - Lesson drawn: Large disparity in route choice numbers; O-L-D emerged as a low choice route.

4. **Decision for the Current Round:**
   - Other drivers noticed regret-driven inefficiencies and might correctly predict mass migration back to the cheaper route, O-L-D.
   - With such a saturated spread on O-R-D last round and proven cost inefficiency, a return to O-L-D is the sensible move assuming less crowding.

5. **Strategic Consideration:**
   - With this pattern, drivers learning from high regrets might swing toward O-L-D more heavily; wise gains likely lie in lower expected congestion.
   - Anticipate route distribution adjustments; additional insight to test into O-L-D for favorable cost prospects.

Based on this analysis, to optimize cost benefits and aim for a lower regret outcome, the recommended route choice is:

```json
{"route": "O-L-D"}
```

1. **Review of Previous Round:**
   - You chose route O-R-D.
   - Route choice distribution was 16 drivers on O-R-D and 2 drivers on O-L-D.
   - Your regret was 130, suggesting that opting for O-L-D would have been 130 points cheaper.

2. **Cost Calculations for the Previous Round:**
   - **For O-R-D:**
     - Fixed cost on O-R: 210.
     - Variable cost on R-D: 10 * 16 = 160.
     - Total cost: 210 + 160 = 370.

   - **For O-L-D (based on regret):**
     - With a regret of 130, the cost for O-L-D was 370 - 130 = 240.
     - Fixed cost on L-D: 210.
     - Variable cost on O-L for 2 drivers: 10 * 2 = 20.
     - Total cost: 210 + 20 = 230.

3. **Understanding Regret:**
   - The regret points to O-L-D being significantly cheaper due to lesser congestion with only 2 drivers choosing that route.

4. **Decision for the Current Round:**
   - Given the significant regret and the crowding on O-R-D, moving to O-L-D can reduce costs, as it had much lower congestion resulting in smaller costs.
   - It's expected that other drivers might also notice this pattern and could attempt to shift to O-L-D, balancing the distribution.

5. **Strategic Consideration:**
   - Anticipate shifts in driver behavior as they react to incurred regrets. It would be wise to preemptively adjust to avoid future costs driven by large congestion.
   - Selecting O-L-D should capitalize on the expected benefits of potentially lesser crowding.

Given these considerations, the recommended route to target minimized costs is:

{"route": "O-L-D"}

During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-L-R-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To make an optimal decision, we'll need to evaluate each available route and its associated costs, considering the potential distribution of all 18 participants. Here are the detailed steps:

### 1. Evaluate Each Route:

#### A. Route O-L-D:
- **Cost on O-L:** \(10 \times X\), where \(X\) is the number of drivers choosing this segment.
- **Fixed Cost on L-D:** 210.
- **Total Cost for O-L-D:** \(10 \times X + 210\).

#### B. Route O-L-R-D:
- **Cost on O-L:** \(10 \times X\), where \(X\) is the number of drivers choosing this segment.
- **Fixed Cost on L-R:** 0.
- **Cost on R-D:** \(10 \times Y\), where \(Y\) is the number of drivers choosing this segment.
- **Total Cost for O-L-R-D:** \(10 \times X + 10 \times Y\).

#### C. Route O-R-D:
- **Fixed Cost on O-R:** 210.
- **Cost on R-D:** \(10 \times Y\).
- **Total Cost for O-R-D:** \(210 + 10 \times Y\).

### 2. Decision Strategy:
- **Determine Distribution:** Ideally, avoid the route most participants will likely choose to minimize variable costs.
- **Expected Distribution:** Participants may favor direct routes, such as O-R-D, initially due to its simple fixed-cost structure.

### 3. Cost Considerations:
- **Avoid High Congestion:** Choose a route where fewer drivers may go, reducing personal cost due to pricing on variable segments.
- **Flexibility in Choice:** Consider that O-L-R-D can distribute costs across O-L and R-D strategically if it's less favored.

### 4. Choose Strategic Route:
- **Speculate on Choices:** With a more complex new option (O-L-R-D), initial rounds may see fewer participants choosing it due to unfamiliarity.
- **Potential Choice:** If O-L-D is expected to be crowded and O-R-D usually attractive due to its simplicity, O-L-R-D might prove a testing ground for less competitive dispersal.

Based on this strategic evaluation, it may be optimal to choose:

```json
{"route": "O-L-R-D"}
```

This strategy provides flexibility and adaptability based on congestive patterns observed from adjustments other drivers might make. This choice considers the balance of cost efficiency and the probability that others might ignore this route compared to the more straightforward options like O-L-D and O-R-D.

  - **Cost on O-L:** \(10 \times 17 = 170\).
  - **Fixed Cost on L-R:** 0.
  - **Cost on R-D:** Since all must pass through R-D at 17 drivers, \(10 \times 17 = 170\).
  - **Total Cost:** \(170 + 0 + 170 = 340\).

- **For O-R-D (1 driver):**
  - **Fixed Cost on O-R:** 210.
  - **Cost on R-D:** \(10 \times 1 = 10\).
  - **Total Cost:** \(210 + 10 = 220\).

### 3. Understanding Regret:
- Since your regret was 0, and given the route's popularity and cost experience, O-L-R-D delivered an optimal experience relative to collective traffic patterns.

### 4. Decision for the Current Round:
- **Reconsider Participation Patterns:** The extreme majority (17) took O-L-R-D, deviating from it might be risky if it was optimally chosen.
  
- **Predict Adjustments:** Given the normal tendency for drivers to follow successful strategies, O-L-R-D will likely remain congested unless significant insights change its dynamics.

- **Considerations for O-L-D or O-R-D:**
  - O-R-D provides very low base cost when less in use, but distribution suggests heavy influence due to competitive insights or congestion experiences.

### 5. Strategic Move:
- Expect potential shifts due to the discovery about O-R-D being extremely unpopulated in contrast.
- To mitigate risk and account for heavily used routes possibly shifting dramatically, change to:
  - **O-R-D:** Potentially cost-effective if players skewed by past choices remain on O-L-R-D.

Given this scenario and potential redistributions or behavioral changes, the calculated decision focused on achieving lower costs unseen the prior round lies with:

```json
{"route": "O-R-D"}
```

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

### Strategic Considerations:
1. **Distribution Insight:**
   - If more drivers choose O-L-D, the cost per driver increases on O-L due to congestion.
   - Conversely, if more drivers opt for O-R-D, the cost increases on R-D.

   - Without prior knowledge of distribution, it’s crucial to balance between routes with less historical congestion if this is an early round.
   
3. **Cost Balancing:**
   - The key is to choose a route with a lower expected number of participants to minimize the variable cost per segment.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```
